function loginButtonBoot() {
    if (!window.FB && typeof FBboot == 'function') FBboot();
    if (!window.gapi && typeof googleBoot == 'function') googleBoot();
}
$('.login').click(function(e){
    loginButtonBoot();
    $('#loginpopover').toggle();
    $('.login').toggleClass('btn-primary');
    e.preventDefault();
});
$('body').click(function(e){
    if ($(e.target).closest('.login-button').length) return;
    $('#loginpopover').hide();
    $('.login').addClass('btn-primary');
});

    <h1 class="heading hash-target h1 mart0 pad0">
<span class="offset"><a id="top"></a></span>

<span class="heading__t">
Hardest Routes</span></h1>

</div></div>

    <div class='regions__read '><div class="regions__inner ">

<div class="article readable">


<a rel="prev" href="/en/article/rocktypes"><span>Rock Types and Geology for Climbers</span></a>
<a rel="next" href="/en/article/hardesttradroutes"><span>Hardest Trad Routes</span></a>




<p>The history and development of rock climbing is marked and driven by the ascension of ever harder climbs. Pushing the limit is what drives climbing, attracts the media and the public and thus opens even more opportunities for development and progress.</p>


<p>This progress started more than hundred years ago with the first ascent of a 6a (<a href="/climbing/germany/sachsische-schweiz/schmilka/area/227382078">Teufelsturm</a>, Elbsandstein, Germany in 1906), the first 7a+ (5.12a, <a href="/climbing/united-states/the-black-hills/route/2074671534">Thimble</a>, North Face in South Dakota, USA) and the first 8a in 1977 (<a href="/climbing/united-states/devils-lake-state-park/route/17532535">Phlogiston</a> by Pete Cleveland).</p>

<p><a href="/climber/wguellich">Wolfgang Güllich</a> then pushed the line further with the first 8c (<a href="/climbing/germany/frankenjura/krottenseer-turm/route/17885701">Wall Street</a> in the Frankenjura in 1987) and the first 9a (5.14d) with <a href="/climbing/germany/frankenjura/waldkopf/route/17885275">Action Directe</a> in 1991.</p>

<p>2017 marked the year the first 9c (5.15d) was freed by <a href="/climber/adamondra">Adam Ondra</a> (<a href="/climbing/norway/mid-norway/route/1425664191">Silence</a>) in Norway but also the first female climbed a 9b <a href="/climber/angyeiter">Angy Eiter</a> with <a href="/climbing/spain/malaga-sevilla-area/route/1088393466">La Planta de Shiva</a>.</p>


<p>Around the world new super hard climbs and boulders are being established and freed at an unprecedented pace. What better place to track these routes, their first ascensionist and repeaters than the world’s largest rock climbing and bouldering platform.</p>


<p>theCrag’s advanced search allows you to create any list of routes, by style, region or grade. As an example we provide you here with the link to the search filter for the <a href="/climbing/world/routes/with-gear-style/sport/assert/is-not-project?sortby=grade,desc">world's hardest sport climbs</a>. Feel free to play with the filters, find the hardest routes in your country or - if you think something is missing or wrong - just fix it by <a href="/en/article/contributing">contributing</a> to theCrag.</p>
